They are already making tonnes of money from<br>\r\n&gt; selling subpar products compared to what their competitors (AMD, Apple) are<br>\r\n&gt; offering of late. What motivation do they have to improve things for their<br>\r\n&gt; customers? Pyramid schemes<br>\r\ninvolve people; on the primes of payments or<br>\r\nservices for enrolling others into said scheme.<br>\r\n(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyramid_scheme" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyramid_scheme</a>).<br>\r\n<br></blockquote><div>I agree with you on the hoarding progress bit. My use of the term "pyramid scheme" was mostly for dramatic purposes and that it rings the term "fraud!" in most people\'s minds. My main point is that Intel has on average access to the same amounts of resources and talent pool as Apple and AMD. It is difficult to explain why Apple and AMD have made such monumental advances in chip technology in a comparatively short period of time. Maybe Intel got too comfortable with being a "market leader" and stopped paying attention to competition. It will be quite interesting to watch how they try to make a come-back and as you said, chip consumers stand to benefit the most.</div><div><br></div><div>CHEERS! <br></div><div><br></div><div>Martin.<br></div><div> <br></div><blockquote style="margin:0px 0px 0px 0.8ex;border-left:1px solid rgb(204,204,204);padding-left:1ex" data-o-mail-quote-node="1" data-o-mail-quote="1">\r\nIs it intentional though.
